<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> Im a daily shaver, and this thing saved me so much time every morning. Self cleaning base is a great feature. change filter regularly. Best results on dry face, with the grain.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve had this shaver for two and a half weeks and I&#x27;m returning it.  I shave my entire head, except for a goatee, and my testicles.  I was hoping for a quicker shave than I get with a regular 3-blade manual safety razor.      First off, it wound up taking longer than a manual razor.  The one wide foil is not well suited to shaving a round skull and it takes a lot more passes to run the razor closely over all areas.  Maybe the three floating heads of other brands may be better at covering all the spots.    Second, the edger doesn&#x27;t shave as closely as the blades, so to shape my beard I had to continue to use the safety razor if I didn&#x27;t want the areas around the beard to be scruffier than the other parts of my face.    Third, it shaves my testicles OK, but the the shaver really stings the seam between them.    With extra effort I could get a decent shave.    It gets an extra star for the liberal Panasonic return policy.</li>
    <li> This was my first attempt to use an electric shaver after about 10 years of conventional shaving. The shaver is unable to give me a clean shave especially around the curvy area just below the chin. I tried both dry and wet modes but couldn&#x27;t get it to do my job. Applying more pressure causes a pain on the skin. If you are looking for a clean shave this is not the one. Next I&#x27;ll probably try philips or go back to conventional:(    The trimmer and self-cleaning features are good but main functionality is broken, so doesn&#x27;t matter.</li>
    <li> I have been using an elecric razor since I was sixteen and I&#x27;m well itno my fourty&#x27;s now.  My father was a big Remington fan so I used that brand of shaver for many years.  Then we got him a Norelco (Rotary) for Christmas one year and he loved it, so I switched to Norelco too.  I had problems with both shavers in terms of skin irriatation but they did the job on my sensitve skin. Well, my last Norelco started losing power so I thought I would upgrade.  I always wanted one of those fancy Braun&#x27;s with the automatic cleaning/lubrication system but they are well over $200 -I did not want to upgrade that bad! In searchng Amazon for an alternative, I saw the Panasonic.  The Panasonic products I&#x27;ve owned in the past have worked well, so I was open to the idea of a Panasonic shaver.    Ordered and received the  shaver in a very timely manner from Amazon.com and plugged it in for a charge. Gave it a try the next morning and I was immediately impressed. I like the weighty and substantial feel this razor has in my hand.  It&#x27;s also a good looking tool (always important).  After a few days of using this razor my face was smooth and free of nicks or bumps.  WOW!  this thing really works!  My face experienced zero irritation as a result of switching to this new razor.  The micro fiol from Remington and the rotaries always chewed up my face until I got used used to them (translation:  until I wore down the razores a a bit).  but I had no irritation at all with the Panasonic.      The cleaner is a bit bulky and noisey and there&#x27;s really nothing slick about it; in fact its kind of ugly, but it works well!  I set it to clean/charge/dry my razor and it came out sparkling new and shiny clean.  Replacement blades, screens, and cleaning cartridges are fairly reasonable in price, so that is good.  I also shaved using shaving foam but the results were not so good when I did.  The foam gobed up the razor so it did not cut as closely as it could have.  In fact, I was lsft with some pretty nasty stubble.  I then began using Lab Series pre shave and once again I was extrememly impressed. I know that&#x27;s another review but the point I am making is that you should get the best pre electric shave lotion (not foam) you can (avoid the drug store stuff if possible).  Lab Series is great and has very low odor.  It&#x27;s about [...] a pop but it lasts a long time and works better than any other pre electric shave lotion I&#x27;ve tried.    I am completely happy with this shaver and highyl recommend it.</li>
    <li> This is a great product.I am 60 yrs. old and have shaved with a blade ever since I began to shave.Of course I have tried an electric razor a few times,but they never got anywhere close as a blade.Over the years I have had several skin cancers removed from my face and head creating a surface that is none too pleasant to shave with a blade.About a month ago,I told my wife that I was going to try one more electric razor.After reading up on different razors and looking at the reviews,I decided to try the Panasonic.Best decision I have made in a long time.I use it in the wet mode and lather up with shaving creme just like I was going to use a blade.  My face comes out as smoothe as a baby&#x27;s behind.All I can say is try it,you will love it!!!!!!</li>
    <li> Razor give a close shave and it only took it a month to train my beard to be cut.  Great Shaver.</li>
    <li> I don&#x27;t think I need to spend a ton of time giving this the lauds and laurels it deserves, but it does deserve them.  This was my first experience with a wet/dry razor, and it works very well.  It is a bit louder than the electrics I&#x27;ve had in the past (I think this is due to the exceptionally fast rate the blades move at), but if you use it in the shower the noise isn&#x27;t as bad as you&#x27;d think.  I guess the bigger concern is the extra water wasted if you shave in the shower.    Back on track, almost as smoother as with a regular razor, but without all the extra irritation on the neck.  Best electric I&#x27;ve used (I&#x27;ve had braun and norelco models in this similar quality/price range and this is the best so far).</li>
    <li> I have a very tough beard.  Usually, I have to shave with an electric razor first and then use a blade to finish it up.  I have been trying different razors of all brands and costs for years, and nothing ever worked.  Until now.  This razor is incredbile.  Even if I don&#x27;t shave for a few days, it takes off everything clean and smooth.  And I don&#x27;t need to touch up with a blade afterwards.  I am still shocked how well it works.  In fact, this is the only review I have ever written on anything I purchased.  That is how much I like this.</li>
    <li> It is a solid product.  Close shave.  Quiet compared to my past electric razors.  The cleaning process takes about 45 minutes after each use.  No complaints after using it for about 30 days.</li>
    <li> What I find remarkable is that over 200 people gave this a favorable review.    What you might do before buying is to consider why over 30 people disliked it so much that they left a negative review.      I&#x27;m such a sucker.  I read so VERY MANY reviews, on this site and others, and I looked into all the \\&quot;technology\\&quot; that goes into the shavers.  The concept and the name behind a thing does not make it an improvement.  Whatever special shaving angle or cleaning technology the electronics companies might hawk as the latest thing might not translate into a better shave.    In my case, I&#x27;m coming from using a regular non-electric razor.  I wanted something that I could just pick up and shave with -- it would have to be fast and it would have to work both wet and dry.    I got this shaver and tried it for about four weeks, wet and dry, many different configurations.  It never worked for me.  As other reviewers have said, it worked on parts of my face well but not others.  I developed new areas of razor burn on my face (even in the fourth week) that I never had before.  Also, I didn&#x27;t like having some places on my face being shaved so close that it seemed like I shaved UP with a razor, while others seemed not fully shaved.  So immediately after the shave I&#x27;d look sort of hacked up.  This look would be accentuated after a few hours of growth.  Also, to get even this poor quality of shave, I&#x27;d have to go over and over all areas of my face.  It took me about three times as long as shaving with a normal razor, despite the fact that when I shave with a normal razor I have to get wet, wash my face, use shaving gel and after shave, etc.      I just cannot understand the 200+ positive reviews.  This thing actually works for some people??  Incredible.      Well, my plan was to try it for 30 days and return it if it didn&#x27;t work, and that&#x27;s what I did.  Amazon return was very easy. (My reason for return: \\&quot;Does not work as advertised.\\&quot;)    As for noise, cheap feel, and so on I agree with other negative reviews, but honestly I wouldn&#x27;t mind if it were twice as loud and felt like a toy, so long as it could shave my face.  Using a razor takes a fraction of the time and my face looks evenly and closely shaved every time.</li>
    <li> I purchased this razor specifically for the purpose of shaving my head and I have to say that I am glad I did!  I have been using it for about 4 month&#x27;s now and it works great.  If you like the bald look but do not like using a regular razor on your head, then give this a try.  I use it with either Williams Lectric Shave or Shave Secret shaving oil.</li>
    <li> The Vortex ended up being exactly what I thought it would be... A solid razor with a self contained cleaning unit for a decent price.    I don&#x27;t have much to add to the other reviews about the actual function of the razor.  Long story short, it works.  You may have sensitive skin or may not take well to an electric, but that&#x27;s not the razor&#x27;s fault.  I haven&#x27;t had any issues yet.    My only complaint (the reason for the 1 star loss) is how loud and how long the cleaning process was.  I&#x27;ve never had a self cleaning unit, so I really didn&#x27;t know what to expect, but I figured the cleaning/drying cycle would take like 20mins tops.  It was well over that, pushing about an hour.  Also, it&#x27;s a bit loud if you have it near your bed (mine&#x27;s on the bottom shelf of my nightstand) or anywhere you wouldn&#x27;t want to hear it.  About the sound of somebody&#x27;s loud vibrating cell on a glass table.    Anyway, certainly not enough for me to make a return, I&#x27;ll just keep it charged ahead of time and will put it in to clean when leaving for work in the AM.</li>
    <li> I finally switched from blades. I love this thing. I have been using it for 4 months so I can so for sure I am a convert. I can shave faster and get a great shave. I bought a high end Remington to leave at the gym and it is a joke compared to the Panasonic. I thought the self cleaning was a gimmick, but it it great.</li>
    <li> I have been searching for a good shaver for my head and face for years. I shave my head bald, and my beautiful face, lol. I have used many electric shavers over the years, even Braun for my head and face. This Panasonic ES8109S saves my head  as close a razor blade. You cannot get any closer than this shaver for a nice smooth shinny head. I read reviews, researched and found many men recommend this Panasonic. Amazon had the best price, and free shipping, how can you go wrong?     <li> This shaver is absolute trash. To put it simply it does not shave at all, leaving behind huge patches of hair on my neck, underside of my head and also on my face. The only part of my face that it will actually shave well is my mustache or about 10% of the total area of skin I need to shave. I used it every day for three weeks and the results did not get better.     <li> I purchased this shaver a year ago, and while I have traditionally preferred blades, I thought I&#x27;d give this one a try due to the positive reviews.      After a year, I am reasonably pleased with the performance.  I use it in a \\&quot;dry\\&quot; fashion, and the shave quality is good.     <li> I normally don&#x27;t write reviews, but I tend to benefit from them and this gadget blew me away. I&#x27;ve tried and failed over the years to find an electric shaver that could do the job as well as a razor. I thought it was physically impossible. Not so, as I came to find out. I am in the military. We shave everyday, and the old saying goes \\&quot;a good soldier never needs a shave/haircut). This means you should always look clean shaven. I have coarse whiskers densely arrayed around my chin, with a light sprinkling elsewhere. This gives the appearance of someone attempting to start a goatee when the five o&#x27;clock shadow comes in. Like Joe Dirt, it&#x27;s genetics. It also means I can&#x27;t get away with a crappy shave, it makes the Joe Dirt effect much more pronounced.    I&#x27;ve always used razors, usually a variation of the Sensor. I must be getting old because a vibrating safety razor with half a dozen blades that costs as much as car payment is not attractive to me. Said razors did the job well, but at a price. There is always a tradeoff. I tried different strokes and techniques but the end result was always the same - I would get razor bumps. To add insult to injury, some days I have to be up fairly early for physical training. This means I have to be clean shaven, but I don&#x27;t want to shower first because I will get sweaty and have to shower anyway, which makes softening the coarse whiskers a dubious process at best because I am drowsy and in a hurry. This means shaving nicks in addition to ingrown hairs. Though I&#x27;ve grown proficient in the use of tweezers, the process grew tiresome. I thought there could be a better way, without lathering up and forgetting to pick up more razors when I run out.    The hair on my face grows in one general direction, the ones at the base of my neck go in all directions of the compass. This shaver deals with them all nicely. The package arrived, I had everything out and ready to go and charged up in no time.    I understood that this was a wet/dry shaverand I thought it would be a good idea to wet my face and use a thin cream to lube my mug for the big event. I turned it on and pressed it to my face and felt some pain with hairs pulling. I had a three day growth. Lesson one, use this for one or maybe two days&#x27; growth at most (for me, your mileage may vary). Lesson two, don&#x27;t try to get fancy and use conventional shaving preparation methods. I used to mock this product, but get some Lectric Shave. It smells like old school aftershave and supposedly stands your whiskers up for the shave. I don&#x27;t know if mine are standing up any more than usual, but it provides a lubricating quality to your skin which prevents razor burn when you have to go over the same spot several times, which you will be doing if you get any electric shaver. It works. I no longer deal with ingrown hairs, razor burn or nicks. Shaving (the actual act of removing hair) takes a few minutes longer, but it is well worth it and you don&#x27;t have to do all the prep work, so in the end I would guess that this is actually quicker. After shaving I can bathe and wash my face and there is no burn where I shaved, even with soap on the same area. This is certainly a more flexible and forgiving arrangement. I&#x27;ve had this product for three weeks. The first few days I was not convinced, and even the product literature will tell you to stick with it. They were right.    A 100% charge would appear to last for a while, I&#x27;ve not really tested it. When I begin it says 100%, when I send it home to clean up it still says 100%.    On to the self contained cleaning system. I run it through a cleaning cycle everyday after shaving. I imagine it may reduce the life of some components, but it&#x27;s cool as hell to have a machine do my dirty work for me. I shave, slap the shaver into the cleaning/charging unit and walk away. When I need it later it is dry and clean, even on the inside. I&#x27;ve checked. I will not bellyache about a few bucks for a detergent cartridge once in a while, butthat&#x27;s me. If I get tired of doing that, then I can get analog and run it under tap water. Both will do the job.    In summation, if you have similar grooming issues to deal with, you can buy this with confidence. No I am not a paid endorser, I&#x27;m just excited that I found a better mousetrap.</li>

    <li> I switched over to this model of electric shaver last week because I was sick and tired of spending 15 dollars on 4 gilette fusion razor blades that were only lasting me 4 shaves before destroying my face.  Knowing that Panasonic shavers were available for using wet with lotion, and having tried one dry (which I was decently impressed by) I decided to take the plunge and order this thing for 100 dollars.    1st Shave:  Ouch.  I was excited as a kid on christmas when this thing got to my house, and made the mistake of attempting to shave with it dry, since I didn&#x27;t have time for a shower.  It did a fine job on my face.  My neck looked like somebody had tried to lynch me, and it took about 4 days for the cuts and the razor burn to heal.  My fault though, even back when I used a Norelco it was a cool skin model and I didn&#x27;t use it unless I had just showered.  That left me with razor burn too.  Disappointed, I figured I&#x27;d wait it out to see what happened.    2nd Shave: WOW!!! Well, after waiting three days for my face to heal up, I showered, splashed on some lectric shave, and mixed some Edge Advantage Revitalizing Cream with an even amount of Neutrogena razor defense shave cream and had at it.  Face was WAY smoother in a short period of time.  The neck still burned, but this time I was prepared with post shave lotion and that helped out greatly.  Also, allowing the lectric shave 30 -45 seconds on the neck and face before applying the cream helped me get a LOT closer on the sides of the neck, under the jaw, and on the face.  I was pretty happy with that shave, and thought that once my neck, and particularly my adams apple got used to it, this thing would be awesome.  So I went looking for slicker, longer lasting shave gels and other things to help set my beard up, leading me to shave 3.    3rd Shave:  This one wasn&#x27;t as good as the second, but not as bad as the first.  After buying some neutrogena razor defense face scrub (for use before shaving) and some Nivea For MenHI-PERFORMANCE X-TREME shaving gel I figured I&#x27;d have the winning combo nailed.  Wrong.  The foam was thick, which I&#x27;m sure gunked up the blades resulting in me having to go over my face and neck more, resulting in more irritation.  To make matters worse, that pre-shave scrub only seemed to dry my skin out, which coupled with some razor bite and an alcohol based pre shave did not end well.  I did, however, notice that despite how my neck FELT, it looks like it&#x27;s improving with every shave in terms of adapting to the irritation.  Still not \\&quot;AS CLOSE AS A BLADE WITHOUT THE IRRITATION!!\\&quot; like so many of these companies claim.      I will probably come back to this review later to update it, but for now all I can say is that the performance of the shaver is EXTREMELY important to me, over aesthetics, cleaning systems, and all that other stuff.  My beard isn&#x27;t super thick, but it&#x27;s definitely thick enough to ware down Gilette Fusion blades by the third shave, and after the fourth the blade is useless.  That said, after just a shower and either of the previously mentioned shave creams(neutrogena or edge advantage) I was getting the most absolutely perfect shave you could think of or envision.    In comparison, I am still letting my skin get used to this.  I&#x27;ve had this new shaver for a week, and I&#x27;ve used it three times.  My skin DOES seem to be adjusting, but it seems to be extremely important that you first have the razor cleaned, as the shaving solution also acts as a kind of lubricant, or so it seems.  Second, DON&#x27;T use this thing dry if you have issues with electrics beating up your neck.  My old norelco did this, and even the perfect gilette fusion nicked my neck every now and then at the adams apple, same spot this thing is having issues.  Thirdly, use a thin shaving cream or gel that stays slippery.  Clinique and Billy Jealousy, as well as Zihr, are all supposed to have great ones that provide excellent razor glide, although they are expensive, and I haven&#x27;t yet tried them.  Edge advantage seems to no longer be in production, which is unfortunate.  Neutrogena razor defense cream has worked well for me though.  Thin is important though, as a thick gel will clog the razor. Fourth, a pre-electric solution like Lectric Shave, Afta, or any of the others out there seems to make a difference.  I can&#x27;t feel it on my skin until after the shave when I notice how much smoother my face is compared to when I don&#x27;t use it. Lastly, get a really really good soothing after shave balm.  Neutrogena&#x27;s isn&#x27;t bad, but it doesn&#x27;t cool.  Nivea is supposed to have a good cooling one, and again Billy Jealousy is supposed to have good after shave balm as well.  If you feel like spending 22 dollars on it, I have heard rave reviews for the clinique post shave healer.      Ultimately, I bought this razor to save money on fusion blades, which are costing me a reasonable chunk of cash.  That and the fact that I love different electronic gadgets and this thing fit the bill and sounded great, so I took the plunge.    It is NOT as thorough as a razor in my opinion, nor is it as fast.  That said, I have still only had it for 6 days, and have only used it three times.  Stubble seems to grow back quicker, which would infer the shave isn&#x27;t as close.  Despite this, my face feels smooth as velvet after use, despite some irritation.  The irritation is a major issue though on the neck and adams apple.  My neck is shaved just fine, my adam&#x27;s apple is tough though, and the razor burn on both afterwards exceeds my face.  In the end though, a good post shave lotion can take care of that quickly.  Cheaper than buying tons of blades, but more irritation if you aren&#x27;t used to electrics.  Also, the money you spend trying to find the right kind of pre shave, during the shave, and after shave lotions could add up quickly.    These are my opinions, everybody has a different beard type, different skin type, etc.  I have a friend who&#x27;s been shaving for the past 8 years with a braun syncro and has no issues with it, and gets close.  He started using it at 14 though and hasn&#x27;t stopped, so I imagine he&#x27;s used to it.  I used a rotary electric from 13 to 15 and then went back to a blade until last week, a little less than two months from my 22nd birthday, and my face is having a tougher time.  But, amazon does give you time to return this thing, so if you want to, try it.  If it doesn&#x27;t work, back it goes, if it does, then you&#x27;re set, so you don&#x27;t have anything to lose.      EDIT:  After the fourth shave I&#x27;ve had enough.  The razor does a nice enough job on the face, but it murders anything below my jaw line.  After two light passes with it on my neck I began bleeding and was left with a big red smile looking mark from one side of my neck to the other.  Again.  Also, with all the passes needed to actually cut the hairs, shaving with this razor took me FAR longer than with a blade, so back to blades I go.  Apparently with a brush, rubbing alcohol, a dry cloth, and a dry place to store your razor you can extend the blade life by two to three times it&#x27;s usual life.  Sounds like that&#x27;s what I&#x27;ll be doing from now on.  I really wanted this razor to be awesome and do what it said it does, but frankly it falls well short. However when using a gel, it shaves super close, and can rub on the skin, which can lead to skin burns. Dry/wet is good enough.&lt;br /&gt;3- The nono technology are phenomenal. I feel its better than shaving with a Mach3 . The skin feels soft after a shave. However, one has to run the shaver over the neck more than once to reach the contour areas. It gets them. Braun didn&#x27;t even come close, no matter how many passes you made.&lt;br /&gt;4- The indicator shows a tap sign when the trimmer needs to be cleaned. Just run it under the tap and whola in 20 secs, the shaver is clean.&lt;br /&gt;5- One negative feature is the inability to shave when the unit is being charged. I guess this is a safety feature.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So overall...A++ for closeness of shave, as good as a blade.&lt;br /&gt;Practical , flexible, looks nice and blows away the competition.     <li> The reason I purchased this shaver was to find a solution to the acne or bumps that I have around my mouth. I previously owned a Norelco with the 3 rotating heads. The acne continued so I had to experiment and switched to a different moisturizer which helped to improve my skin a lot. I believe it was a combination of shaver, cutting technique, post shave product and moisturizer that was necessary to solve my problem.     1. Use shaving gel (not only does it give help the razor glide more easily, it lubricates the blades so that they won&#x27;t get damaged)    2. Do not stretch the skin. This may contribute to ingrown hairs.    3. Shave against the grain, then with the grain. (this ensures the hair will grow the same way and helps to prevent ingrown hairs)    4. After using this for several weeks I&#x27;ve discovered a shaving method that really takes advantage of this wonderful machine.    1) Wash face, leave wet.  Apply shaving cream (I use Edge Gel).    2) Turn on hot tap water.  Turn on shaver, rinse in hot water while it&#x27;s on, then start shaving    3) Periodically dip the (running) shaver under the hot water.  The hot, wet blades melt the gel on your skin and help you to get a really close and comfortable shave.    4) Repeat step 3 until there&#x27;s no more gel on your face, then give it one last good rinse before setting it in for a daily cleaning/charge.  Your cleaning cartridges will last longer because the shaver is already pretty clean when you start the cycle.    You will be rewarded with a pleasurable, close and comfortable shave that compares to going to the barber shop for a hot towel/straight razor professional shave. Unfortunately, the base isn&#x27;t up to spec - the clean cycle simply doesn&#x27;t do a very good job and the controls for selecting what you want the base to do are downright bad.  I&#x27;d buy the razor by itself instead of getting the base with it - just clean it yourself with some warm water and rubbing alcohol.</li>
    <li> I got a very good deal on the ES8109S Vortex, which makes it easier to appreciate. It&#x27;s not perfect, but then again I never found a razor that could shave my thick beard perfectly. I still have a hard time with the neck area, but otherwise it&#x27;s a fine tool. I recommend it.</li>

    <li> This is my third electric shaver in eight years.  My first was a Braun Syncro 7526 (with a cleaning stand), which I bought back in January of 2001.  The second is a Norelco 7885XL, bought in January of 2004.  I wrote a review of both those electric shavers here at Amazon.  Both of them are still working.  The Braun has had its set of foil and cutter replaced a few times over the years.  Basically, I replace my shavers after four years of daily use to upgrade to newer technology.  My newest electric shaver, the Panasonic ES8109S, is the subject of this review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This Panasonic is a versatile shaver.  Unlike my previous electric razors, this one can be used \\&quot;wet\\&quot;.  Basically, you can use it with your shaving cream, just like a regular blade razor.  And like a typical electric razor, you can use it dry.  You can clean it with soap and water, or you can use the cleaning stand.  The 8109S gives you choices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ok, you&#x27;re thinking, \\&quot;This Citan has been using an electric razor for eight years.  I&#x27;ll buy whatever he recommends.  He&#x27;s the new electric razor guru, the next best thing to God.  A Stud among us!\\&quot;.  Now, I appreciate your vote of confidence, but I am no electric razor guru.  And definitely not a God.  Stud maybe . . .&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, what has been the closest shave of the past eight years?  There was a period of about 4-5 months during those eight years when I took a break from the electric razor and tried a Gillette Mach 3.  I started with the typical shaving gel and found that the Mach 3 shave was only marginally smoother than the Braun Syncro&#x27;s.  Eventually, I decided to try using a shaving brush and a shaving soap with the Mach 3.  And that my friends, gave me the best shave of my life!  However, it was also messy and probably wasteful of hot water.  Not to mention the fact that the replacement blades for the Mach 3 were somewhat expensive.  You see, to get the best (and most comfortable!) shave out of a blade razor, you have to replace the blade often.  Once a week, in my case.  Once you feel the razor tugging, it&#x27;s time for a new blade.  So, I went back to the electric razor and have not looked back since.  And no, I do not have the courage to try a straight razor!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This Panasonic shaves better than the old Braun and the old Norelco.  It is the most comfortable of the three.  Perhaps because the ultra-fast blades lessen the chances of the razor tugging on your beard.  The beard gets sheared off before the razor can move.  Hence, you will not even feel the slightest pull.  I wanted to try how the Panasonic will perform when used with a shaving soap.  Using a shaving brush, I whipped up some foam on a mug, wet my face with hot water, and lathered it on.  Under those conditions, the Panasonic gave me the best shave that I can remember.  In fact, I now shave at night, before bed.  The shave is so good that my face is smooth all throughout the next work day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, does it make sense to use a shaving brush and a shaving soap with an electric razor?  Probably not, as that defeats the need for convenience.  Citan would be late for work if he did this in the mornings!.  I will most likely go back to dry shaving very soon.  But I just wanted to see the potential of the Panasonic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;How does it shave dry?  Very good.  The best of any electric shaver that I have tried.  But you will have to try it for yourself.  The ergonomics are fine for me.  If you have a prominent Adam&#x27;s apple, you may be better off with a blade razor.  The larger heads of the electric razors might make it hard to maneuver around your Adam&#x27;s apple.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The cleaning stand is terrific!  The razor comes out clean and recharged.  It also leaves an oily film on the foil for lubrication.  While the razor can be cleaned with tap water and soap, I really do recommend the use of the cleaning stand.  The cutters on this Panasonic oscillates very fast, against the foil.  I am not an engineer, but I suspect the Panasonic has a greater need for lubrication than most other foil razors due to its faster speed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My face did not require any adjustment time to get used to this shaver.  I went from a Norelco 7885XL (rotary type) to this Panasonic with no issues whatsoever.  Maybe your experience will be different.  I have visited many shaving forums and message boards over the years.  And there are some people who will always have trouble shaving, no matter the system they choose.  I hope you&#x27;re not one of those.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recommend this shaving system to anyone who wants to try a new electric razor.  The Panasonic wet-dry shavers are very versatile.er foil razors due to its faster speed.      My face did not require any adjustment time to get used to this shaver.     <li> If you&#x27;re an intelligent shopper you&#x27;re doing some research comparing different shavers and brands. But the Panasonic has several key advantages for you to consider...    1)  Braun&#x27;s \\&quot;superior\\&quot; pulsonic technology makes 10,000 strokes.  Panasonic&#x27;s makes 13,000, for shaving, and a blistering 17,000 for cleaning purposes.  2)  Braun&#x27;s retail price is over twice that of Panasonic&#x27;s.  3)  Braun&#x27;s shaver CANNOT be used in the shower.  The 8109S can.  In fact, it&#x27;s fully immersible, if you feel like shaving underwater! :p  4)  Braun&#x27;s foil is straight, with a flexible head.  The Panasonic&#x27;s head is also flexible, but has a convex foil, which makes shaving under the neck much easier.  5)  Both have a nifty cleaning mechanism for their shavers.  To the best of my knowledge, the only way the Braun dries the shaver is with a heating element.  The Panasonic not only dries your shaver with heat, but also a fan to really air it out.  My shaver is bone dry once the drying cycle is over.  Also, the cleaning solution for the Panasonic is alcohol-free, which prevents breakdown of plastics and water seals.      ...     <li> First, a little background on my shaving history.  I started around 14 with my Dad&#x27;s standard rotary electric shaver, which he claimed was all I&#x27;d ever need to get the job done.  In a sense, he was right; the shaver got the job done, but I now know that it takes a truly great product to get the job done WELL.  I dabbled a bit with blade shaving but found it to be impractical and often painful.  It was just not worth the extra effort to achieve a minor improvement in closeness.  So I did what most men do: Take their dad&#x27;s advice and continue on a path of a daily ritual of mediocrity and indifference.  I used to dread waking up knowing that the task lay before me, just wanting to blink my eyes and have it be over.  No longer.  This product truly did change my whole perspective.    Turning on this razor for the first time summoned a response akin to what an aviation engineer must have felt when he heard a jet engine for the first time...wow.  The 13,000 RPM blades emit a futuristic whir that almost say \\&quot;Shave with me, you won&#x27;t be sorry.\\&quot;  And you won&#x27;t.  This was my first experience with a foil shaver so I was a bit dubious about their supposed performance.  However, that soon passed after my first shave.  I have NEVER had a shave as close or as painless.  The combination of the swivel head that contours over your face with the high RPMs of the blade that capture even the toughest hairs make for an extremely close, comfortable shave.  This thing is what George Jetson uses in the morning before he hops in his spaceship...it&#x27;s that good.  After I shaved with it the first time I could not stop running my hands over my face in amazement, and I still can&#x27;t.  If you&#x27;ve shaved with a rotary your whole life, you will not believe the difference in performance this foil razor gives.  So as to not be long winded, the moral of the story is: Close, comfortable, convenient shave at a reasonable price.  I can&#x27;t compare it to some of the higher end competition, but I can say I couldn&#x27;t imagine getting a closer shave than this (so why pay an extra $100 to test that theory?).    Some Tips I&#x27;ve Learned After 3 Months of Use:  -For the closest, most comfortable shave possible with this shaver, shave after your stubble has had 2 days to grow and shave with shaving gel/cream and hot water like a blade.  I do mine in the shower.  The 2 days of growth allows the shaver to capture the hairs much more easily and the gel helps give a comfortable, smooth shave.  Follow up with an aftershave balm.  I follow this ritual:  After shaving Friday morning, I usually don&#x27;t shave again until Monday morning, after which I get an amazing shave that puts a smile on my face and prepares me to face the challenges of the work week.  -For daily shaves, use a pre-shave solution and shave dry.  This is convenient and allows for maximum day-to-day performance.  -Use the cleaning base after EVERY shave.  When shaving dry, take the foil off and rinse out all the hairs before putting it back into the cleaning base.  The most important thing this cleaning base does to your shaver is LUBRICATE.  If you notice after the cleaning cycle is over, take the foil off and look at the blades in the light.  The liquid on the blades is lubricant, and it will help tremendously to provide a smoother, closer shave as well as preserve the life of the blades.  As a matter of fact, try an experiment.  Rinse the blades and let them dry, then put the foil back on and turn on the shaver to listen to the blades.  Now do the same after the shaver has been through a cleaning cycle.  You will notice that without lubricant the blades actually give off a slight grinding, abrasive sound barely noticeable to the ear.  It is noticeable to the face...trust me.  Always use a properly lubricated shaver when you can.  By rinsing after shaving and then putting your shaver in the cleaning base, you will prolong the life of the cleaning cartridges.  -To best shave the sides of your cheeks along the jawline up the sideburns, I&#x27;ve found that pulling the skin to make it tighter actually doesn&#x27;t result in the closest shave.  Instead, move the shaver over the skin without stretching it.  This makes the skin kind of roll underneath the shaver, then the 13,000 RPM blades make short work of the hairs.    This pretty much wraps it up.  I don&#x27;t usually review products here on Amazon, but I do when I find them particularly noteworthy and I have something of substance to offer consumers.  If you&#x27;re still wondering whether or not to get this razor, take Nike&#x27;s advice...Just Do It.  Your face will thank you.</li>

After many hours of research I thought I wanted another Braun...their top of the line Pulsonic model. Almost bought one based on a few blogs on the web. I did cringe at the asking price of $250 - $300 suggested retail. I have always enjoyed Panasonic products and noticed this razor at half the asking price of the Braun. It seemed too good to be true, but Panasonic products have never let me down yet. I gave it a try, knowing I could try it for 30 days and send it back if unhappy. I had nothing to lose.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have had it a week now and nobody is taking this shaver away from me. I dare you to compare the 2 razors back to back and honestly say the Braun is worth double the price. They are, in my opinion, in the same class. The Panasonic is quieter both shaving and in the cleaning stand. It shaves closer and cuts more hair on the first pass, eliminating a 3rd or 4th pass. The Braun would sometimes knick my adams apple or lip and I have tried to get the Panasonic to do it but it wont (call me stupid). Since I dont have to shave 3, 4, or 5 times on my neck, the razor burn is gone. The ingrown hairs are 99% gone (I have had only one this past week). The cleaning gets the blades cleaner and they smell soapy clean and not chemically clean. The best part, a bonus if you will, is the Panasonic is water-resistant. Not only can you rinse the head off underwater at home or on the road, but you can shave in the shower or use shaving creams or lotions (gels are not recommended). The top of the line Braun can be rinsed under water but not used \\&quot;wet\\&quot; or with creams or lotions. The only drawback I could find is the travel bag they supply. I was hoping they could have supplied a better case to hold the cord and shaver for extended trips. Not a big deal though, on a big trip...I will have a big suitcase so I&#x27;m sure there will be plenty of room in there for a cord.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In conclusion, a great shaver with all the current technology and features offered by the competition at a reasonable asking price.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT - MONDAY JANUARY 21, 2008&lt;br /&gt;Since purchasing, this razor still continues to be my favorite. I have now started using it \\&quot;wet\\&quot; by warming my face with hot water, then applying a Neutragena shaving cream. The results are better. It shaves more hairs on the first pass, the cream eliminates any friction, and gives me the closest shave yet with an electric (some areas of the face feel like I shaved with a blade).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT - SUNDAY JANUARY 18, 2009&lt;br /&gt;Still loving it and using it everyday. However, the wife ran it through the front load washer tonight. It is now very clean. Still runs but needs a new set of blades. For added measure and the price of new blades and foil, I found a really good deal on the ES8228S shaver. The only difference between the two is the ES8228S adds a zippered vinyl travel case (vs cloth bag with draw strings) and the head has independent floating foil (each of the 3 foils is on their own suspension to track the curves of the face better).th draw strings) and the head has independent floating foil (each of the 3 foils is on their own suspension to track the curves of the face better).</li>
    <li> I bought this product for my boyfriend who needs to shave often but was always cutting himself. His old electric left his face feeling whiskery even right after he shaved. Read other reviews about the Panasonic being almost like a razor so I decided to try and he LOVES it.....doesn&#x27;t even mind shaving.     <li> I purchased the ES8109S Vortex after reviewing several brands and reading hunderds of reviews.  First use, perfect shave.  Yes it misses a few hairs under the chin, but I have never owned an electric that didn&#x27;t.  It is the nature of how they work.  A few passes, perfect.      I am shaving my head daily.  It works great in the shower with a little soap.  Smooth as a blade, takes about 4 minutes for whole head.  I would highly recommend this shaver for those who want an electric option for head shaving.  Looks like I&#x27;m getting 5 shaves (face and head) on a charge.     <li> To preface, this shaver is the first electric shaver I&#x27;ve used in probably a good decade. I had a cheapie Norelco years and years ago when I first hit puberty, but I quickly changed to razors. My reasons for doing so were just about the reasons of everyone who prefers razors: My beard grows thick and quick, and within a week I&#x27;ve usually got a good \\&quot;crumb catcher\\&quot; going. Beyond that, razors are just the smoothest shave you&#x27;ll get, even with the risk of nicks and razor-burn.     After finding this on a deal through Amazon, somewhere in the low $90&#x27;s I believe, I felt like it was time to try electrics once again since shaving every other day was a losing battle for me and I had resorted to once a week grooming. I figured for the price, it better be pretty darn good - $90 (on sale) is no small drop in the bucket for me when it comes to this stuff.    Well, I set aside my favorite blade (Mach 3 Turbo for me) and prepared for the worst. Like every new shaving method, it takes about a month for the beard to adjust, and the first shave wasn&#x27;t entirely pleasant (as I recall from my previous foray with electrics a decade ago).     But, now speaking about 4 weeks into it, I can honestly say I&#x27;m impressed. On my cheeks and face, it&#x27;s almost impossible to tell between the razor and Panasonic&#x27;s little beauty. I&#x27;ve tried it in the shower (yes, it is completely waterproof) and with shaving cream and all sorts of lubricants, but for my thick beard I found that it just didn&#x27;t get close enough and took too long with all the water and creams. My favorite method, I&#x27;ve found, is dry shaving at the end of the day/beginning when your face isn&#x27;t so sensitive, and just running the blades under some cold water now and then (both to clean them momentarily, lubricate your skin just a tad, and keep them cool - the blades do get hot) while simultaneously moving it in small circles over the area you want shaved (almost like brushing your teeth).    There are still a few trouble spots underneath my chin and on my neck that are difficult to get without stretching my skin quite a bit, but they were problem areas even when I was using a razor.     What&#x27;s more, and this is definitely my favorite attribute; with the method above there&#x27;s so little irritation (only on the outskirts underneath my chin) that I don&#x27;t feel like I&#x27;ve been mauled by some ravenous feline after shaving! It&#x27;s fantastic. Particularly above the chin, I can barely tell it&#x27;s cutting the hairs, and don&#x27;t feel bothered even during the process.     The base itself fits in a corner, is fairly compact (about the size of one of those scented candles in a jar), and does its job well. The cleaner does not use alcohol to clean, but a detergent solution that uses water housed in a small tank also in the base.    And to top it off, you&#x27;re looking at a cheaper upkeep than blades. The detergent packs are cheap ($15 for a set of 3, each one lasts a month), and you need to replace the foil (once a year, with the blades once every two years (~$50 for both foil and blades). So that&#x27;s $110/year max for shaving, compared to $180/year for cartridge blades.    If there are any Cons for me, it would be the following:    -While in operation it is a tad loud. Not annoyingly so, but it&#x27;s a very high frequency pulsating noise (that you won&#x27;t notice in about 30 seconds into the shave), but afterwards (especially if you shave in a smaller room) everything sounds distorted because of it for about a minute.    -The cleaning base is also a little noisy. You won&#x27;t hear it down the stairs or anything, but if you&#x27;re in the next room and this buzzing keeps coming up, it&#x27;s the base and the shaver cleaning itself.     -The same button that turns the shaver on also turns on the \\&quot;manual cleaning\\&quot; mode if you press it for 5 seconds. This is NOT a shaving mode, but a cleaning mode to use when you don&#x27;t have the base. I have not had any trouble with it accidentally changing modes so far, but the manual does warn that the cleaning modeis not designed for shaving.    Overall, I&#x27;ve had a rather pleasant and refreshing experience with the shaver. While occasionally I may return to razors if I need that ultra-smooth shave (black tie events), this thing is now my bread and butter. It does a grand job once you&#x27;re used to it, and I can&#x27;t imagine going a full week without shaving again. The only area this thing has left to surprise me in is how long it lasts without being recharged as I haven&#x27;t had any extended trips, but I don&#x27;t see it failing me there either (I use about 20-30% of the battery per shave, at about 7-minutes a shave).    I highly recommend it for anyone who&#x27;s looking at an electric shaver and is pondering whether it&#x27;s worth the ~$100 investment. I found it to be.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used Braun shavers for a few years, and prior to that Norelco.  The cleaning system for the Braun always irritated me, due to the evaporation of the solution.  However, it was giving me a very close shave until, I believe, the battery finally lost enough power. The power button certainly is in an odd place where I suspect most men put their thumb when shaving and I did shut it off by mistake once.  To avoid that from happening a minor change in how you holdthe razor is required which is to shift the thumb closer to the head where at least Panasonic thinks your thumb should be.  I like to hold the razor so that it does not touch the palm of my hand and only my thumb and fingers are gripping it but I have tried a golf club grip a few times which worked fine but will take some getting used to.    I have only shaved dry and probably won&#x27;t use it wet, with or without lather. Either way, it will be nice to be able to thoroughly clean it and not have to rely on the dumb little brushes.    All in all I have no complaints about this razor and I would recommend it to anyone who does not expect a shave as good as a regular blade. I will try it for a few more days and then will decide whether its a keeper.   Any suggestions are welcome, as I really don&#x27;t want to return it.</li>
    <li> Been using this shaver now for 2 weeks and I love it!  Used for both the head and face.  Works exceptionally well to shave the head - wet or dry.  As with all electric shavers, it has difficulty with neck hair.  The cleaning system is fantastic - used about every 3-4 days to clean the shaver. An excellent value in this price range. In fact, I would put it up against the $180.00 Braun in all aspects!</li>
    <li> My credentials: 40 yrs. shaving (the 1st 25 years only with a blade.)  I was so obsessed with closeness that I used to shave with a badger brush and shaving soap using a Hoffritz single blade. (This is as close as a barber&#x27;s straight blade.)    I have tried just about all the shavers since then.  Remingtons, Norelcos (through the Bond, James Bond model), all the Brauns through the Activator, and the last 3 or 4 Panasonic models.    Braun, with its interceptor blades, convinced me that shaving electrically was quicker, less bloody, and more comfortable than my blades, along with an acceptable shave.    Panasonic&#x27;s shavers convinced me that shaving with an electric could come very close to the quality of a blade.  However, there was always a problem.  The first few ultrasonics I had had terrible batteries.  Another one went dead after a year (and had the reputation for doing that too).  And the last one (I&#x27;m too lazy to look up that number) was a step backwards and never shaved very close.    I got the ES8109s for around $86 here at Amazon before Christmas and was delighted.  It fit perfectly in my hand, had the closest shave I have experienced so far, was good around the neck, and was comfortable.  I always liked the cleaning system but cleaned and charged my shaver in the cleaner only once a week (every Sunday).  Daily, I would brush out the whiskers.      Unfortunately, after only 3 months, I already felt that the blades needed to be replaced.  After 6 months, I can barely get an acceptable shave at all, having to go over and over the same area and still not get a close shave.  This is not acceptable since (it seems to me at least) Panasonic&#x27;s replacement blade/screens are the most expensive.  The Brauns always lasted me between 18 months to 2 years.    I am now debating whether to give this shaver one more try by replacing the blades or try a Braun 360 instead.  (I refuse to buy the Braun Pulsonic since they feel very cheap in the hand, in my opinion, and have integrated blades/shaver screens that cannot be cleaned out with a brush.)  This is really frustrating since Panasonic makes wonderful shavers but always appears to have an \\&quot;Achille&#x27;s heel.\\&quot;</li>
    <li> Shaves very closely without irritating the skin. Used wet with lather it glides very smoothly but doesn&#x27;t seem to shave any closer than dry, and using it wet takes extra time fussing with lather and cleanup so I usually just pick it up and shave without water. The cleaning unit has a complex cycle that whirs and clicks for over an hour, but it cleans the shaver well. This shaver is much less expensive than the top-end Braun, which I haven&#x27;t tried, but I&#x27;m glad I bought this one as I don&#x27;t see how an electric shaver could perform much better.</li>
    <li> Either wet or dry, this shaver didn&#x27;t do a good job for me.  I wasn&#x27;t able to get a close shave at all.  The last straw was when I did one of those side by side tests.  I shaved with an old dull Gillette razor on half my face and this thing on the other.  The powerless, old blade won hands down.  My wife saw the difference immediately.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The above, of course, were my results and it may have a lot to do with my facial make up.  However, there were other things that I disliked:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- When the shaver is at full charge it blinks all the time.  I found that pretty annoying in the middle of the night if I happened to have the bathroom door open.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- One of the reasons I got the shaver was to save money in the long run on blades.  However, the cleaning cartridge doesn&#x27;t have a long life and would have cost me as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- The cleaning system takes about an hour and is pretty noisy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- I found the shaver screen got hot pretty quickly, even when using it wet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, for me, it didn&#x27;t work too well.  I&#x27;ve shipped it back and gone back to my old blade razor.</li>
    <li> OK, so I have decided to stop being a review parasite (I often look to reviews to help me in buying decisions, but don&#x27;t write my own review).  I have been using the Panasonic E8109S shaver for about a week now, and here is my 2 cents.    1st, in my opinion, based on using two rotary electric razors (Norelco), 2 foil razors (Braun), and now a 3rd foil razor, none give as close of a shave as a razor blade, but if you give your face about a month to adapt you can generally get a good shave from the better (more expensive) electrics.  I prefer the foil razors, as they seem to me to shave closer, and it is easier to maneuver them around the ears and nose without leaving behind hairs.  Now on to the review.    As stated above, I had 2 Braun shavers.  Braun 1 was an excellent shaver that cost around $80 - $100.  It gave a great shave, held a charge for a couple of weeks, and quietly hummed when operating.  It came with the Braun cleaning system.  When it&#x27;s motor failed after a year of operation I bought Braun 2, which was a cheaper razor (around $60 I think).  It didn&#x27;t hold a charge as long, didn&#x27;t have the cleaning system, didn&#x27;t shave as well and was much louder.  The lesson here is you get what you pay for, and name brand doesn&#x27;t guarantee anything.  Luckily  I realized Braun&#x27;s warranty is 2 years, not 1 as I had thought, so I got Braun 1 repaired for free (they even mailed it to me after fixing it) and I got another 3 years or so use before the on/off switch got stuck in the on position, and I started using Braun 2 again.  Needless to say, it didn&#x27;t take long before I was ready to shell out some cash for a better razor.      Initially I was planning on getting another higher priced Braun, but was pulled to the Panasonic by a couple of points.  First, it is cheaper than Braun&#x27;s with comparable features, and I was intrigued by the ability to shave using shaving cream again.  Since the Panasonic sells for $100 (although I got it for $73), I will compare it to Braun 1, which was similarly priced.  I cannot compare it to today&#x27;s Braun models, so you will have to look to reviews of those products, although I doubt they are much different from the model I owned.  It was a 4000 series (I don&#x27;t remember the exact number, but I still have Braun 2, which is model 5770).      Cleaning System:   I much prefer the cleaning system that comes with the Panasonic, as the base is more square, and takes up less room than the rounded Braun base, and more importantly it has rubber feet that keep it in place when the razor is being cleaned.  I had to wedge the Braun cleaner against something, or else it would slide across my sink from the vibrations caused by the razor running.  It also seemed louder than the Panasonic, but since it died a couple of years ago, I may be remembering that part incorrectly.    Ergonomics:  The Panasonic is a clear winner here as well.  Not only is the razor noticeably lighter, it is skinnier, with a contoured shape for easy gripping, and a rubberized handle to reduce slipping.  The bulkier, plastic handled Braun doesn&#x27;t come close.    Noise: Here I have to give the edge to the Braun.  I don&#x27;t think the Panasonic is much louder in Db, but it is much more high pitched, almost like a Dentist&#x27;s drill and hair clippers had a baby, and this is it.  Luckily I find that I get used to the sound about 2 seconds after I turn it on, probably because it is fairly quiet.  It still beats Braun 2&#x27;s roar.    Shave: Again the Panasonic clearly beats Braun 2, but the more aptly compared Braun 1 gives it a run for it&#x27;s money.  I would call this a tie in the dry shave category.  The dry shave was closer than the shave with shaving cream the first couple of days, but it seems to be shaving closer as I continue using shaving cream.  I&#x27;m not sure if this is due to my face adjusting, me learning better technique, or what.  I will say that I love using shaving cream again, and it is worth the miniscule difference that may occur in closeness.  When I finish shaving, my face feels totally clean shaven, and I only notice the difference at the end of the day (stubble seems slightly more pronounced).    Overall, I give the Panasonic 5 stars because it is reasonably priced, gives a great shave, holds it&#x27;s charge for a long time and isn&#x27;t unreasonably loud.  The led that gives the remaining charge in 10% increments is also nice (and puts it in competition with higher priced competitors).  On the negative side, the whine is a bit high pitched, and I cannot find replacement heads or cleaning solution at local stores, so will have to order it online - probably cheaper, but certainly not as convenient.  All that to say I believe this is the best electric razor I have ever owned, and I won&#x27;t hesitate to get another one in a few years when this one inevitably dies.</li>
    <li> I have only used rotary shavers before this one, and always seemed to get burned by them, and my neck would always get ripped up and blotchy red spots, which is really annoying when you have to shave to look clean for work, parties, events, etc.    So I decided to try a foil shaver and see if it worked any better. Well, after using this shaver for almost two months now, I have to say it is the best shaver I could imagine using. I have not burned my neck since I began using it, and it stays much cleaner than my old razor, thanks to the HydraClean System and even the ease of cleaning with running under a faucet. I feel that foil shavers rinse cleaner than do rotary ones, and it is probably purely because the blades are more straight on these, whereas the old rotary shavers I had contained slightly curved blades, and could never seem to get fully clean.    This is the type of shaver a person can use for years, with replacing the foils, of course, and be completely happy with. I would recommend this to anyone that swears by electrics, as it is smooth, comfortable, can work wet or dry, and leaves you with the smoothest shave you can have from an electric. I&#x27;ve never shaved better in my life, and plan on sticking with Panasonic shavers in the future.</li>
    <li> I purchased this shaver to replace my existing 6 year old Panasonic.  I was not disappointed.     <li> The Winner Is...    The Panasonic ES8109S 3-blade - barely. Put the Remington blades and cutter (keeping the center blade of the Panasonic) on a Panasonic 13,000 RPM shaver and you would have the World&#x27;s best electric shaver. The Remington shaved a little closer than the Panasonic and provided a faster shave. However, the difficulty in cleaning, noise and lack of a charging base tipped me to the Panasonic as the final choice.    This is a review of three Panasonic models; ES8243A (4-blade), ES8109S (3-blade) and ES7109, the Remington MS2-390, the Norelco 8260 CC and the Braun Series 5 8995 (8985 &amp; 8975 only differ in displays and cleaning). I have an average beard and have been using electric shavers (foils and rotaries) over 30 years. The models here are no better than any of the other higher quality shavers I&#x27;ve owned. It takes about 10 minutes (no shaver will give you a first-pass close shave) to get to that good dry shave (with or without pre-electric gels/oils) and you do have to put pressure on to get a close shave. This means recharging every 4-5 days. Gels/oils do make the process easier - not faster - and I have reviewed six of them on their Amazon sites.    ES8109S: This 3-blade shaver gives a very close shave, with some work. It does give off a higher pitch &#x60;whine&#x27;, while shaving, that is somewhat annoying, but is not what I would consider noisy. Nor is the cleaning operation noisy. Based upon other reviewers, I was expecting it to sound like a lawn mower, but it is just an occasional buzzing noise as it cleans. The \\&quot;Arc Foil\\&quot; design slows shaving (see discussion, below).    ES8243A: I had hoped that the four blades of the Panasonic ES8243A just might be able to give a superior shave. As it turns out, the large four-blade surface is like trying to keep the end of a 2x4 on your face. It makes cutting in the areas where you don&#x27;t have a lot of skin area (chin, jaw line, upper lip, base of sideburns, etc) more difficult. In fact, I think that the fourth blade in the middle actually interferes with a better shave and these two middle blades are not as good as the primary cutters. The \\&quot;Arc Foil\\&quot; design makes it even slower (see discussion, below). Another future problem with the 4-blade system is that you&#x27;ll want to buy a new shaver when your blades and foil need to be replaced. What kind of an idiot is going to spend 80% of the cost of a new shaver just to get a set of new cutter blades and foil? All in all: the ES8243A 4-blade is a poor value.    ES7109S: The flat design of the foil is a better design than the \\&quot;Arc Foil\\&quot; (see below). Unfortunately, this shaver has an under-powered motor and the floating head that cannot be locked.    Panasonic discussion: Panasonic had developed an outstanding shaver line some ten years ago. My old ES8067 still shaves closer than this new \\&quot;NANO Technology\\&quot;- a misnomer (marketing gimmick). I think the reason is that Panasonic&#x27;s older models came with cutting blades with the individual blades having been about half the width of all of Panasonic&#x27;s newer cutting blades (including replacements). This means more surface area on the newer blades and that means less cutting. Remington has the ideal blades (that Panasonic used to make) and it shows in closer cutting and less time spent doing so. Additionally, these new Panasonic \\&quot;Arc Foil\\&quot; shavers have the foil curving AWAY from your face at the ends of the foil, further decreasing exposure to the blades and requiring many more passes to cover the same area. Unfortunately, Panasonic puts their better motor (13,000 RPMs) only on these ill-conceived \\&quot;Arc Foil\\&quot; designs. Battery time on the Panasonics is the shortest of all shavers reviewed here. The Panasonic trimmers are so narrow, on all of these models, that you will not be able to trim sideburns with one attempt. You will have to re-position the trimmer to get what you missed. This increases the probability that you will get an uneven sideburn.    The Remington MS2-390 has the blades that thePanasonics should have (and did have years ago): flat foil area (not \\&quot;Arc Foiled\\&quot;), good length (25% longer) and ultra thin cutting blades. As a result, closeness of the shave is better and time spent is shorter. This is, however, the loudest (and it is loud) of all shavers and there are no bells and whistles. Using a pre-shave oil/gel will gum up the blades, as with any shaver, but these blades pop off with even the slightest brushing so be prepared to watch them fall into the sink with every cleaning attempt. A charging stand would greatly increase the convenience of this shaver. Remington did a poor job with the details.    The Braun Series 5 8995 tries hard (you can hear noticeable slowing when necessary pressure is applied, like a lawn mower when it reaches thicker grass), but it doesn&#x27;t get quite as close as the Panasonics or Remington without leaving a stronger burning sensation after the shave. The Braun can also leave burn marks and even cuts (nose and lips) that will bleed. Odd: you would think that, with it getting so close as to actually burn the skin, it would also give a closer shave. I suppose this is proof that shavers cannot \\&quot;lift\\&quot; hairs to cut better. Additionally, the design of the handle is inferior, making positioning more difficult. It does have a much wider trimmer and longer battery life between charges, though.    The Norelco 8260 CC: I used this rotary-type of shaver for many years during the 80&#x27;s. I switched to foil and found I could get a closer shave. This is still the case. Additionally, because of the circular blades, it is somewhat difficult to target certain spots for cleanup. However, this is the quietest shaver.    PS: don&#x27;t accept the nonsense about giving your face 30 days to adjust, unless you are coming off a blade. If you are accustomed to an electric shaver, you only need a week or two to determine the difference. The only thing magical about 30 days is that you can no longer return it for a refund - what a coincidence!</li>
    <li> I bought a refurbished ES8109 shaver on Ebay.  So far, after 2 weeks of using it, I&#x27;m thrilled.    I&#x27;ve been using electric shavers for over 15 years.  During that period, I&#x27;ve almost exclusively used rotaries.  However, I kept buying new ones because they either broke, shave quality wasn&#x27;t good, etc.  I was most recently using a Norelco shaver (Speed XL I think) with a jet clean unit.  I never was crazy about the shave it gave me, and the cleaning unit was messy and eventually stopped working.  Very frustrating.  I liked having a cleaning unit, so I decided to give the Panasonic a try.  With my very first shave I could tell a huge difference.  A nice close shave with little to no irritation.  It even worked well the tough spots (like on the neck).  My face never felt so smooth.  I also love being able to shave in the shower again (all the wet/dry shavers I&#x27;ve used in the past died in 1-2 years, hopefully not this one).  And the cleaning unit was awesome.  Easy to use, not messy like the Norelco one, and it even dries the razor.  The cleaning solution is pretty cheap on Amazon too (about $10 for a 3 month supply).    One suggestion.  I&#x27;ve been using shave oil (try American Crew, or Kiehl&#x27;s Shave Oil) and it&#x27;s worked very well. I tried shaving one day with Edge Gel, and maybe it shaved too close.  I ended up with a lot of irritation, even drew some blood in places.  My face felt like it was burning.  I went back to the shave oil again, and voila, another great shave.</li>
    <li> As the title mentions spending higher than average on a product doesn&#x27;t always mean you will get a higher than average product. And in my opinion the Panasonic ES8109 is one of those cases.    For the positives:  Very fast smooth motor, much more comfortable shave overall compared to the $30 shavers I have used in the past. It comes with a built in trimmer to edge up around hairlines/etc which is always a plus, but even standard on the cheaper models. The LCD display is neat and gives an accurate measurement of the battery life remaining in which I start to charge it around 10%. Speaking of charging it does come with one of the fancy smancy self cleaner&#x27;s &#x27;ala&#x27; more profit for Panasonic on accessories(need&#x27;s cartridges).    For the negatives:  Honestly, I could swear I&#x27;ve gotten a closer shave with the Panasonic ES4026NC ($25 Shave mind you). The upside of the ES8109 is that is does to a better job at getting neck hairs, but still has yet to impress me. For the most part I have to work at it to get most hairs, about 95% at best. It still cannot get all of them and this is the biggest downfall on top of the OK quality shave, really nothing to brag about on this shaver. Also the first cartridge didn&#x27;t even last the whole month, and this was after hearing someone being able to use it twice over. I reinserted the cleaner cartridge to see if I could get more out of it but ran into a couple problems. The first being that yes, the cartridge was really used up, after it was done &#x27;cleaning&#x27; quite a bit of hairs were still around the razor. Secondly, the station will not let you select the clean option once it recognizes a dirty cartridge. All in all on the clean/charge station, I honestly think its a waste of a plug and money on cartridges. And as a funny little side note, the adapter plug does make an annoying high pitched squealy noise. Of course it&#x27;s not loud and is inaudible probably more than 4 feet away in a quite room, but still, sounds like cheap parts to me.    Andthere you have it, take my opinions as you will but I just find for the price this shaver sells at, far exceeds what it can actually do. Like I said it isn&#x27;t all bad but at the end of the day I rate this shaver as  \\&quot;It&#x27;s OK\\&quot;.</li>
    <li> My husband has very sensitive skin and he is pleased that it does not irritate his face. He says that it works best when used with shaving cream.     <li> I have been using the Panasonic ES8109 for about 7 months now.  Prior to this I was a Norelco user for nearly 25 years.  Why did I decide to try something different?  I found that over the last 10 years or so the quality of the Norelco products and the shave I received were both decidely in decline.  Even right out of the box, the Norelco shave quality was marginal, and my face still felt like 100 grit sandpaper after working it over for 5 minutes.  The Panasonic was an entirely different story.  I have always used a dry shave, and the Panasonic gave me a smooth shave in the same amount of time.    I use the Panasonic hydrasonic cleaning device that came with it whenever the shaver gets around a 60-70% charge on it, which in my case is about 5 shaves.  It still is giving me a great shave.  The sideburn trimmer does a better job than the Norelco and operates at a higher trimming speed.  I am on my third box of cleaner inserts for the cleaning unit, and each insert seems to last about 3 weeks.  I bought the replacements through Amazon.  The unit restores the shaving head unit and screen to their original condition.  I have not noticed any deterioration of the blades so far, unlike the Norelco that seemed to fade after 4-5 months and you had press very hard to get even a marginal shave!    I would recommend this shaver for a good, close shave.  I&#x27;m impressed with the quality of workmanship.</li>
    <li> I almost never write reviews, so why am I writing one now ? Because I think a lot of people will benefit from what I have to say. I&#x27;ve been using the Norelco Spectra 8894XL rotary for years. I guess if it&#x27;s good for 007 it&#x27;s good enough for me. Movie advertising really does work. Before that I was a blade person. I still use the blade occasionally when I want a smooth shave.     The Norelco never could come close to the blade even with the Spectra set to the closest shave setting. So why did I go to the electric shaver. Speed and convenience. Don&#x27;t need to worry about packing shaving cream when I fly. It still always took at least 6 minutes for the Spectra to do a reasonable job. Three to four years ago, when I had to replace the Spectra blades I thought I would take a look at the foil shavers. I went on to Amazon and read the reviews. There really did not appear to be a major difference between the rotary and foil products. Each had enough offsetting pluses an minuses so I didn&#x27;t really see a clear winner. I stayed with the Spectra.    Finally , a few weeks ago my Spectra battery died. I opened up the case, saw that the battery was basically soldered to a circuit board. Thanks a lot Norelco. Time to look at some alternative options. First thing I did was go to Amazon. They have the most thorough reviews for these types of products on the web. Reviews from a lot of other web sites are basically copy and pasted from Amazon. After I read the reviews, and looked at the distribution of ratings, it appeared that the Panasonic foil product line was getting consistently higher reviews vs other foils and the rotaries. When you see the number of reviews rated 5 or 4 vs the number at 1 or 2, and the 5/4&#x27;s outnumber the 1/2&#x27;s by almost 9 to 1, it&#x27;s time to start paying attention. And this wasn&#x27;t just for the Panasonic foil I bought, which was the ES8109S, but all of the Panasonics were getting consistently high reviews. One recommendation, Amazon, is you should come up with anaverage rating number. Just helps a little, especially if there are a large number of reviews.    I settled with the ES8109S. Best price for the features and technology, including the cleaning unit. Just $20 more than the bare bones shaver. If the cleaner becomes a pain, just don&#x27;t use it. For $104 on Amazon, it was worth a try. Got the shaver yesterday. I read the directions. Panasonic needs to hire some better technical writers. Their instructions are in a treasure map format. It&#x27;s all there, but you need to cipher to break the code. Just a few more sentences and better organized layout,  and I think they could sell more units, especially if people download the manual before they buy a product. I have an advanced engineering degree and it still took me an inordinate amount to time to figure out what the hell they were talking about. What&#x27;s a \\&quot;course\\&quot; ? Replace that word with \\&quot;sequence\\&quot; and use some other American English words in some other instances and the manual will be more readable. Panasonic, hire some good American English technical writers. Please.    Finally, I set up the shaver and the cleaner while heeding all the warnings delineated in the manual. Nothing blew up or smoked, or spilled. That was a good sign. Charged the unit overnight and tried it out in the morning. I was more than impressed. How can I make up for all the time I lost using the stupid Spectra ? It took me less than half the time, under 3 minutes, to get a shave that was far better than what the Spectra will ever be capable of, and that&#x27;s coming from a foil \\&quot;virgin\\&quot;. FYI, I don&#x27;t have a very heavy beard, but enough to frighten the cat in the morning. Face burn, not a problem with this unit. The shave rivaled the blade. Rotary users, take a look the this Panasonic line next time you&#x27;re in the market. The learning curve is non-existent. I was a little reluctant making the change to a foil, and I&#x27;m glad I switched.</li>

The Braun&#x27;s solution could last for 3 months usually.     Panasonic also claims that the foil and cutting block should be replaced every 12 months. That combo costs $50 (from the manufacturer, could be cheaper through another source) whereas the Braun block and foil were good for 18 months and cost around $40-45 dollars to replace. Not a huge difference, but perhaps something to consider.    Also, it sounds like some others here have had issue with the durability of these shavers. I thought my Braun&#x27;s run of almost 5 years was pretty decent. Hopefully the Panasonic can make a similar run.    Conclusion:  Given the results of the shave so far, I am thoroughly impressed with this product. Everything feels like it was made from quality materials with high standards of construction.  I haven&#x27;t used the cleaning station yet, I just charged the razor with the cord the first time.  A full charge took about an hour.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First Shave:&lt;br /&gt;I purchased a lotion style shaving cream, it wasn&#x27;t cheap but I&#x27;m willing to spend a few extra bucks if it makes a difference.  You don&#x27;t need a lot of foam or cream, just a light wet coat to give your face a slick feel.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The big difference is in the shaving technique.  With a regular razor you make 1-2 passes and move on, otherwise you risk razor burn (at least for me).  With the Panasonic I found that you can go over the same spot 2-3 times and from different directions to make sure you don&#x27;t miss anything.  You really don&#x27;t have to worry about razor burn as long as your not pressing hard.  I used slight pressure and a smooth long motion like you would normally use, but I did this in 3 directions.  My face feels like the shave was nearly as clean as a razor shave, but with zero irritation.  I think after 2-3 shaves I&#x27;ll have a pattern down that works for my particular beard growth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning was a breeze.  I just rinsed the shaving cream off of the head with hot water and held the power button until the razor went into it&#x27;s 17,000rpm (you hold the power button down for 5 seconds for this) cleaning cycle.  I turned the razor off added a little hand soap to the screen and repeat the cleaning process.  When I was done I removed the screen, rinsed it out and shook off any excess water.  I then rinsed off the exposed blades, shook off excess water, and took a towel to it briefly to remove any visible moisture and set it on the counter to dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;I really haven&#x27;t found any at this time.  I will probably hook up the cleaning station this weekend to see how it works.  It takes up some counter space so I&#x27;m not sure if I&#x27;ll keep there or not.  It seems to me that I will spend just as much time cleaning the cleaning/charge station as I would just cleaning my razor by hand after each use, but I&#x27;ll give it a shot and see if I like using it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Conclusion:&lt;br /&gt;So far I&#x27;m very impressed with the quality of this razor and the comfortable shave it provided.
