It would do a sorta ok job on the face and cheeks although no semblance of being as close as a blade but refused to cut the long hairs in the neck.  So I would use that as a first shave and then touch up the rough spots in the shower with a blade.  Why even use an electric at all?  Also because of my sensitive skin by using the blade, I had to skip shaving the next day.  About four or five years ago, I tried a Braun Syncro shaver, a foil type like the Panasonic.  Where it cut, it cut closer then the rotary but left huge gaps, particularly on the neck and I never could seem to get all the hair no matter how many passes I made.  So I was skeptical that the Panasonic, another foil shaver would really be better.    From the first day I used this shaver, I knew it was going to be my best electric razor ever.  Mowed right thru the hair getting most in the first pass and I shaved my entire face all within a a couple of minutes.  Did a great job on the neck as well although the hair was not too long to begin with as I had shaved the previous day.  The heads look somewhat similar to the Braun Syncro but for whatever reason, the performance difference between the two is like night and day.  In the ensuing four days, it has only gotten better.  Already my neck has become de-sensitized enough so I know I&#x27;ll be able to shave every day.  After I finish, it feels in most areas as close as a blade although truth be told, it&#x27;s not quite because the five o&#x27;clock shadow creeps in a bit earlier in the day then it did when using a blade.  However as mentioned, I can now shave every day and I think I could shave more then once a day if needbe, something I never thought would be possible.    The biggest drawback?  The NOISE!  It whines like a little jet engine!  It is be far the loudest shaver I have used, louder then the Braun and way louder then the Norelco rotary.  I live in a condo with my bathroom wall facing another unit and I really hope the noise is not bleeding thru.  That is something Panasonic needs to work on and I think I will let them know about it.  That is why I&#x27;m cutting back on my rating a bit.  Performance wise I&#x27;d give it a solid four and a half stars.    I just used the cleaner setup tonight and it did a fine job.  I don&#x27;t see the need to use it every day.  I just tap the hair out after each use and I think using this setup just a couple times a week will be fine.    If my mind changes significantly after more use, I&#x27;ll edit my review.  Things I want to try is a wet shave in the shower and to skip a day and see how it handles the extra growth but right now I&#x27;m happy I bought the razor as long as the noise isn&#x27;t bothering my neighbor.</li>
    <li> This electric razor will shave you close to a blade razor.  You don&#x27;t even feel it cutting.  At first I thought that was weird after using a Nokia Series 7 with rotary blades.  The Nokia always left my skin irritated due to constant running of the razor on one spot to get all the hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic will get them with 2 or 3 runs.  You can run it deeper and more if you want to get the closest shave and it will not irritate you.  It&#x27;s simply amazing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some additional features are water based cleaning base (cheaper refills), super accurate sideburn trimmer, and nice display.  This razor&#x27;s price is also a winner.  To my understanding it shaves as good or better then high end Brauns or Nokias, but it has half initial and ongoing costs.</li>
    <li> After 1 month of using this shaver, I&#x27;m convinced it is the best I&#x27;ve ever used. I&#x27;ve been using a Norelco 8865 XL for several years now, and I was pretty happy with it. But if I had to shave 2 days in a row, it was a very uncomfortable experience, with a lot of irritation on my neck. And I also have always used a foil type shaver, currently a Remingtom Titanium and earlier a cheaper Braun, because I couldn&#x27;t use the 8865 to square off my sideburns with a nice straight line, or get a couple spots under my nose and lower lip. The Remington gave a decent shave, but it would actually draw tiny dots of blood around the edges of my mouth, which is a bit too close for comfort. I&#x27;ve found one shaver that does it all in the Panasonic 8109. I think it&#x27;s amazing. I&#x27;m not sure why, but this shaver does not irritate my neck area at all. I don&#x27;t mean less irritation than the other 2, I mean NONE! I really can&#x27;t feel a difference on my neck where I did and didn&#x27;t use the razor. And the shave I get is nice and close. I&#x27;ve never used a blade in my life, so I have no idea how it compares, but it shaves me as close as any shaver I&#x27;ve ever used. This is a shaver and not a magic wand, so it does require several passes to get a clean shave. But I believe anybody who complains that it doesn&#x27;t shave clean with 1 pass has just never used electric before. I&#x27;d love to hear about the electric shaver that can shave clean in one pass, I don&#x27;t believe it&#x27;s possible. And I also feel that the poor craftsman blames his tools, and this tool will allow a very good shave when used correctly.  As for the self cleaning stand, I&#x27;m less enthusiastic. It does work as advertised and is a nice addition, but if price was my biggest concern I would get the lower model Panasonic without the HydraClean. I got mine for $108, minus a $30 instant rebate so it only cost $78. The next model down was $79 with no rebate, so taking the HydraClean version was a no brainer. And it is a cool little toy that does work well, it just isn&#x27;t a necessity like with the Braun 360. You can put some soft soap into the heads &amp; let them clean themselves because water can&#x27;t hurt this shaver, unlike the Braun.   In conclusion, I&#x27;d say the number 1 reason I like this shaver so much, is because after 30 years of hating shaving and the irritation I knew I was going to feel, I actually don&#x27;t mind shaving any more. Shirt collars don&#x27;t cause discomfort because the skin feels fine. And shaving 2 days in a row is no longer a dreaded experience, it is actually okay. I would give this shaver 5 stars, but the battery life is a little shorter than my Norelco and I&#x27;m saving that 5 stars for a magic wand that I can just wave over my beard and it disappears.</li>

Anyhow, after a quick review of the top of the line shavers from various manufacturers currently available (including the new Braun Pulsonic models), I opted to go for the latest offering from Panasonic. Even though the new Brauns cost $100 more than the Panasonics, their motors are still slower, and you still can&#x27;t shave with &#x27;em wet. For the uninitiated, higher motor speed &#x3D; faster moving blades &#x3D; less friction &#x3D; less irritation. Panasonics have consistently had the highest motor speed available in any electric shaver.    I&#x27;ve shaved with the new ES8109S shaver for a few days now, and my first impression after the very first shave was that I got a very close shave (consistent with the performance of my prior Panasonics) and, try to understand this, my face did not FEEL as though I had just shaved. It may sound a little odd, but you know how your face feels sensitive to the touch after you typically shave? Well, that sensation, at least for me, was far less apparent after shaving with the new Panasonic. Heck, maybe it&#x27;s the new curved blade and foil assembly that reduces irritation or something. In this respect, the new ES8109S actually outperforms Panasonic&#x27;s prior top of the line offering (the ES8078) and actually causes even less shaving irritation than that model (which itself wasn&#x27;t all that irritating to begin with). Also, much like the prior models, the little pop up trimmer on the side of the new shaver is great not only for trimming sideburns (which I actually never use it for), but also for capturing those awkward little hairs that lie flat or may be becoming ingrown. The latest model is also quieter than the last model and has a more substantial feel to it while holding it.    Oh, one more thing, the ES8109S comes with Panasonic&#x27;s latest iteration of its Vortex Cleaning and charging base, which is slightly different from its prior models, but appears to use the same cleaning cartridge. The Vortex quietly cleans, lubricates and even fully recharges your shaver for you (alternatively, you can just plug the power cable for the Vortex directly into the shaver to recharge it). The cleaning/lubricating solution in the Vortex consists of a slender cartridge containing a detergent based solid that becomes \\&quot;activated\\&quot; when it mixes with water in the Vortex base. The cleaner is not alcohol-based, so it does not evaporate over time like the Braun cleaning solution does - along with the money you&#x27;ll spend on their big, expensive refills.     In summary, I highly recommend the Panasonic ES8109S shaver to persons like me with sensitive skin that is prone to irritation (I know you&#x27;re thinking, \\&quot;Why didn&#x27;t he just say that from the outset?\\&quot;) Hope this review helps!     LONG TERM UPDATE! - Well, I&#x27;ve had 8109S for almost one full year now and it&#x27;s still going strong. I&#x27;ve noticed it&#x27;s become slightly less efficient at capturing the few hairs on my cheeks that tend to lie flat, so it&#x27;s about time for the annual changing of the foil, which I know (based on past experience with Panasonics) will restore the shaver to its fullest hair capturing &amp; cutting potential. One tip I have about cleaning the razor - I shave and rinse clean my shaver every day, and I only clean it in the Vortex when it needs charging which, for me, is about once every two weeks. This cuts down on the usage of the cleaning cartridge. The need to clean your shaver will depend in large part on what you shave with (I use a foam, which tends to rinse cleaner than creams and gels). Also, one more tip regarding the cleaning cartridges in the Vortex cleaning system - you DON&#x27;T HAVE TO replace the cleaning solution at the manufacturer recommended interval. You can definitely get away with using them longer. I tend to use them until the service light on the Vortex base turns on, then I change the cleaning cartridge and water in the Vortex and it&#x27;s good to go. I&#x27;m only on my third cleaning cartridge in the year I&#x27;ve owned the razor.    EVEN LONGER TERM UPDATE! - Well, it&#x27;s a little over a year-and-a-half since I purchased this shaver, and it has died on me. Now, I could try to have this thing repaired for some astronomical price, only to have it stop working again.
